< review>
One of my favorite bookstores in SF! A lovely little independent bookstore that has a good variety and awesome staff picks. My absolute favorite part of Browser Books is the Sale section and the Blind Date with a Book section ($5 each) because it’s an awesome way to try books for cheap that I wouldn’t have otherwise grabbed! Would highly recommend stopping by when you’re looking to pick up a good read!</review>

< text>
I have gone to the Browser Books for 2 decades; buying books for myself, my family and friends. The location is also fantastic, next to Peete's coffee shop and close to my favorite boutiques such as Rag and Bone and Paige and Alice and Olivia and Restaurants such as Ten-Ichi and Delfina and Florio. Browser books is the perfect example of a neighborhood book shop with friendly staff and outstanding selection of books!</text>

< Review>
El Patron is one of my favorite fast food Mexican restaurants. They have a daily special (usually a Chico burrito) that will fill you up in a very tasty, fresh and reasonably priced way. They offer the typical Mexican dishes (tacos, enchiladas, burritos and more), all of which I'm sure you would enjoy. Take out is available, as well as eat in. Try it!< /Review>

<Rating>5<//Rating><Text>Wow!! 🤩
Wife and I brought our three kiddos here (ages 9, 12, 13). Arianna was THE BEST. Our family of five will be back soon and often.

Growing up working a small family business in a small town has basically wrecked my expectations for customer service. I am dreadfully disappointed with customer service everywhere I go. Arianna and the staff at Fresno Coin Gallery are more than a breathe of fresh air.

Immediately upon entering, we were greeted with friendly smiles (behind face masks, of course). Despite showing up just before closing, they gladly stopped pulling inventory so we could look around. Arianna made us feel like we were welcome to stay as long as we liked as she helped educate us and instill some curiosity in our kids.

We left roughly 10 minutes after closing (sorry!) with three very happy kids carrying new coin books and a handful of old coins. It looks like the whole family has a new hobby! I expect we’ll be back after our next payday. And the next. And the next... Searching for old treasures with the kids is a nice break from the TVs, phones, and video games.

I wish I could leave a better review for the kind people at Fresno Coin. My silly words don’t do it justice. I am a HARD customer to please, and I have very high expectations. This place doesn’t disappoint.< /Text>< pictures>

<text>Halu classic with wheat noodles was excellent - noodles were all dente.  Service was quick. <UserId.>100797868570624370697<//UserId.><user_name>George Kokai</user_name><time>1520979226611<//time>< rate>
3<//rate>
<text>Honestly, this wasn't my favorite. I've toured a number of ramen joints in the south bay, and was excited to try this because of online reviews and a friend's recommendation.

First, the karaage chicken was tasty, but I'm personally not a fan of chicken breast meat, which can tend to dry out. The chunks were also a bit large and thick for my taste. Perhaps if the pieces were halved in thickness, I would have enjoyed it more.

Second, I found the ramen broth to be a bit oily/greasy/fatty. I'm not sure which best describes it. It was nice and rich, but was just not ideal for my tastes.

That being said, if I was a drinker, I'd come back. They have an excellent lunch deal with a beer. I also loved the bowl size choices...which I wish more places would offer. I would actually give this place 3.5, if I could.< /text><Pics>None< /Pics>< resp>

Tantanmen! This bowl of ramen is one of my favorites in the Bay Area. Halu is great because everything is über customizable: white or wheat noodles, thick or thin noodles, broth can be less salty, less spicy, etc. I can't vouch for much else on the menu. I tried the shio ramen once and while it was fine, it didn't excite me the way tantanmen does. I went back to tantanmen and haven't looked back. Two stars for the willingness to at least taking it back and giving me the Halu ramen. Turned out that wasn't any good either. It was like ramen in boiled water with some salt added. Does the chef take a quick taste of their food before they serve it? Oh and the rice. It used to be sooo good, full of flavor and texture, and the rice was just the right chewiness. What i had today was mush, with some pork thrown on top. None of the sauce from the pork made it to the rice. This place is not cheap either. They now take credit cards, when they used to take cash only. I suspect there's been a change in ownership. Otherwise i cannot explain the precipitous drop in quality. Don't go here.< /review><pics>None< /pics><Resp>None< /Resp>< Gmap_id>

<review>3.5 stars
I started with the non fried croquettes. It was a bit soft since it was literally just mash potatoes with some panko (bread crumbs). I don't think it's worth the $7.20, but it was an interesting appetizer.

I decided to order the Halu ramen with whole wheat noodles. I thought it would be a novelty to try whole wheat noodles, but they turned out quite flavorless. The noodles don't seem to absorb the broth very well. The broth also turned out to be too oily for me. The bowl only came with 1 piece of chashu although it was quite a tasty one.

The ramen comes in small, medium, large, and extra large. I believe medium is quite sufficient for lunch, but if you are really starving then large is doable.

I think I would come back here to try out their other ramens since all the ingredients were really fresh. The Halu ramen just didn't hit the right spot.< /review>< Rate>

< Text>
The last time I was here, I got a super snappy server. Even his coworker had to apologize for his attitude. Minus stars for that. JERK -__-

The ramen is good. The broth is heavier than other places around the area, with bits of saturated fat floating on the surface of the broth. But it is very flavorful. The noodles are  delicious if you pick the right combination for your taste buds.

My go-to ramen is the tan tan ramen with kurobuta pork. Spicy fans, this will not fail you.

Be wary of service and the wait time. Otherwise, it's an enjoyable experience.</Text>

<userid>103294836369308791982<//userid><name>Chloë Prud'homme Olivari<//name><Time>1362785738907</Time><Rate>4<//Rate>< text>
Chef Kumao Arai and Vincent Kyi combine Tokyo and Yokohama styles to create unique and fantastic bowls of rāmen. Located in San Jose, Rāmen HALU proposes 5 recipes served with original or whole wheat thin or thick noodles elaborated by Chef Kumao:

- Shōyu rāmen: a traditional clear broth blended with their original shōyu sauce and dashi broth served with Chāshū (tender seasoned pork), Menma (seasoned bamboo), Ho-rensou (boiled spinach), Ao-negi (green onion), Naruto (fish cake) and Nori (dried seaweed)

- Shio rāmen: an other clear broth blended with homemade shio sauce and dashi broth. Toppings: Ao-negi (green onion), Goma (roasted sesame seeds), Komi-yu (original onion, garlic and ginger flavored oil) and Nori (dried seaweed square)

- HALU rāmen: is the signature dish that uses Tonkotsu broth blended with shōyu sauce and dashi broth.
Toppings include Chāshū (tender seasoned pork), Menma (seasoned bamboo), Ho-rensou (boiled spinach), Ao-negi (green onion), Kikurage (wood ear mushroom) and Nori (dried seaweed square)

- Tsuke-men (dipping rāmen): The noodles are served separately and enjoyed by dipping them in a rich Tonkotsu broth blended with sweet and sour shōyu sauce and dashi broth. They are thoroughly boiled then washed, leaving the noodles tender and silky. This way, you fully taste the brown sugar, the vinegar, and the spiciness of Shichimi (Chili powder with Seven Japanese spices). Once you have finished your noodles and toppings, add the “Wari Soup” (clear broth) to give your leftover dipping broth a more balanced and drinkable taste.
Toppings: Chāshū (tender seasoned pork), Menma (seasoned bamboo), Ho-rensou (boiled spinach), Ao-negi (green onion), Kikurage (wood ear mushroom), Goma (roasted sesame seeds) and Nori (dried seaweed flakes)

- Tantan-men (Japanese version of dan dan noodles, a Sichuan specialty): Tonkotsu rich broth blended with shōyu sauce, dashi broth, a plash of Japanese vinegar, rayu (chilli oil) and chi-ma-jyan (white sesame paste).
Toppings: Niku Miso (seasoned ground pork), Tenmen-jyan (miso paste), Menma (seasoned bamboo), Ho-rensou (boiled spinach), Ao-negi (green onion), Kikurage (wood ear mushroom) and Nori (dried seaweed square)

Prices are very affordable: from $5.90 for a small bowl of Shōyu rāmen to $14.40 for the special large Tsuke-men (4 sizes are available).
At Rāmen HALU, all the soup stocks and dishes are made from scratch with natural, high quality, fresh local ingredients and Japanese special cooking process.
They never contain MSG (Monosodium glutamate, also known as sodium glutamate)  and all the toppings are prepared fresh on a daily basis.<//text>
